{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_011WQHZiLH8MVzxdYZMzK2M4","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now let me see where the chip structure is allocated and zero-initialized. I can see that at line 3043, `chip = kzalloc(sizeof(*chip), GFP_KERNEL);` is used, which zero-initializes the structure. This means when the chip is first created, all fields (including polling_mode and poll_count) are set to 0.\n\nBut when we resume, we don't re-initialize these fields. This is the problem!\n\nLooking at the flow:\n1. During first init (azx_first_init): The chip is kzalloc'd (zero-initialized)\n2. During suspend: azx_suspend is called, which calls azx_stop_chip(chip)\n3. During resume: azx_resume is called, which calls azx_init_chip(chip, 1)\n\nThe issue is:\n- azx_stop_chip sets chip->initialized = 0\n- But it doesn't reset chip->polling_mode and chip->poll_count\n\nSo if chip->polling_mode was set to 1 before suspend (due to a timeout), it will remain 1 after resume!\n\nThis is the bug. The solution should be to reset chip->polling_mode and chip->poll_count (and possibly other state variables) either in:\n1. azx_stop_chip - before stopping\n2. Let me trace through what happens:\n\n**Initial Boot:**\n1. Chip is kzalloc'd → polling_mode = 0, poll_count = 0, single_cmd = 0 (or from module param)\n2. azx_first_init is called\n3. azx_init_chip is called → chip->initialized = 1\n4. Everything works fine\n\n**First Suspend:**\n1. azx_suspend is called\n2. azx_stop_chip(chip) is called → chip->initialized = 0 (but polling_mode and poll_count stay as they are)\n3. Since chip->initialized was 0, azx_init_chip proceeds (doesn't return early)\n5. chip->initialized = 1 again\n6. Everything should work fine... but the state variables polling_mode and poll_count might not be reset!\n\n**If there was a timeout before suspend (setting polling_mode=1):**\n1. Before suspend, chip->polling_mode = 1 and chip->poll_count > 0\n2. During suspend, azx_stop_chip is called but doesn't reset these\n3. During resume, azx_init_chip is called but doesn't reset these\n4. Now on the resumed system, chip->polling_mode = 1, so the driver starts in polling mode immediately\n5. This could cause issues\n\n**Multiple Suspend/Resume cycles:**\n1. Each time, if a timeout occurs, single_cmd is set\n2. If polling_mode was set, it never gets unset during resume\n3. Specifically: (1) chip->polling_mode is set to 1 when a codec response timeout occurs, but is never reset back to 0 during resume, causing the driver to remain in polling mode after wakeup; (2) chip->poll_count is incremented on timeouts but never reset during resume; (3) chip->single_cmd is set to 1 as a fallback when communication errors occur, but is not reset during resume, preventing proper reinitialization of the CORB/RIRB command interface on the resumed hardware. The suspension calls azx_stop_chip() which sets chip->initialized=0, and resume calls azx_init_chip(chip, 1) which re-initializes hardware, but this flow does not reset the fallback mode state variables (polling_mode, poll_count, single_cmd). After multiple suspend/resume cycles where timeouts occur, these variables accumulate in fallback mode states, causing the sound card to operate with degraded communication modes (single_cmd, polling) that produce choppy audio after resume. The fix requires resetting chip->polling_mode and chip->poll_count to their initial values (0) during azx_init_chip when full_reset=1, and ensuring the CORB/RIRB command I/O is properly reinitialized even if chip->single_cmd was set to 1 by error recovery.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":2,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2353,"cache_read_input_tokens":60653,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2353},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"22d891e9-d25b-4e87-aa08-66013ffbac4d","uuid":"422b0953-03da-494b-b2ab-987cdc226775"}

Specifically: (1) chip->polling_mode is set to 1 when a codec response timeout occurs, but is never reset back to 0 during resume, causing the driver to remain in polling mode after wakeup; (2) chip->poll_count is incremented on timeouts but never reset during resume; (3) chip->single_cmd is set to 1 as a fallback when communication errors occur, but is not reset during resume, preventing proper reinitialization of the CORB/RIRB command interface on the resumed hardware.
